- **Colon:** The second clause explains or elaborates on the first. This fits perfectly — the "unexpected result" IS that the control group outperformed the experimental group.
- **Semicolon:** Simply joins two related ICs without specifying the relationship.

The colon is preferred because the second clause IS the explanation of the "unexpected result."

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Colon — correct and preferred.
- **B)** Comma splice. Wrong.
- **C)** Semicolon — grammatically acceptable but less precise than the colon. The ACT prefers the colon when the second clause explains the first.
- **D)** Dash — acceptable for emphasis, but the colon is more standard for this explanatory relationship.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 19: Colon vs. Semicolon — When Both Are Grammatically Correct**

> The architect's vision was bold **;** the building's design challenged every convention of modern urban planning.

A) NO CHANGE
B) bold, the building's design
C) bold: the building's design
D) bold—the building's design

**Strategic Analysis:**

- "The architect's vision was bold" → IC
- "the building's design challenged every convention of modern urban planning" → IC

The second clause does NOT directly explain or elaborate on the first in the way a colon requires. Instead, it provides a related but separate observation. The relationship is one of **addition or continuation**, not explanation.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Semicolon — correct for joining two related ICs.
- **B)** Comma splice. Wrong.
- **C)** Colon — the second clause doesn't explain WHAT the bold vision was; it adds a related point. The colon is less appropriate.
- **D)** Dash — adds emphasis, but the semicolon is more standard for this neutral joining.

**Answer: A**

**Key Principle:** Use a colon when the second clause explains, illustrates, or elaborates on the first. Use a semicolon when the clauses are simply related but the second doesn't explain the first.

---

**Problem 20: Colon with a Quotation**

> The professor's advice was simple **:** "Read widely, think deeply, and write often."

A) NO CHANGE
B) simple, "Read widely, think deeply, and write often."
C) simple; "Read widely, think deeply, and write often."
D) simple—"Read widely, think deeply, and write often."

**Strategic Analysis:**

- "The professor's advice was simple" → IC (complete sentence)
- "Read widely, think deeply, and write often" → A quotation (not a complete sentence, but a direct quote)

A colon can introduce a quotation after a complete sentence.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Colon — correct.
- **B)** Comma — acceptable in some style guides for introducing quotes, but the ACT prefers the colon after a complete sentence introducing a quote.
- **C)** Semicolon — not used to introduce quotations. Wrong.
- **D)** Dash — not used to introduce quotations. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

#### PROBLEM SET 4: DASHES AND PARENTHESES (5 Problems)

---

**Problem 21: Dashes for Emphasis**

> The discovery—**one that would revolutionize the field of genetics**—was made almost by accident.

A) NO CHANGE
B) one that would revolutionize the field of genetics,
C) one that would revolutionize the field of genetics;
D) one that would revolutionize the field of genetics

**Strategic Analysis:**

The underlined portion is a **middle comma clause (MCC)** / nonessential appositive that interrupts the main sentence: "The discovery was made almost by accident."

MCCs can be set off with:
- **Commas** (standard)
- **Dashes** (emphatic)
- **Parentheses** (de-emphasized)

All three are grammatically correct. The question is whether the dashes are appropriate here.

The phrase "one that would revolutionize the field of genetics" is a significant, impactful detail. Dashes add emphasis, which fits the dramatic nature of the statement.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Dashes — correct and appropriate for emphasis.
- **B)** Single comma — an MCC requires punctuation on BOTH sides. A single comma is wrong.
- **C)** Semicolon — cannot be used to set off a nonessential clause mid-sentence. Wrong.
- **D)** No punctuation — the MCC is not set off at all. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 22: Parentheses for De-emphasized Information**

> The expedition (which lasted **three months**) yielded remarkable findings.

A) NO CHANGE
B) three months,
C) three months—
D) three months;

**Strategic Analysis:**

The parenthetical "(which lasted three months)" is a nonessential clause. Parentheses are used to de-emphasize information — to present it as supplementary rather than central.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Parentheses — correct.
- **B)** Single comma — needs matching punctuation on both sides. Wrong.
- **C)** Single dash — needs matching punctuation on both sides. Wrong.
- **D)** Semicolon — cannot be used inside a parenthetical. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 23: Dash at the End of a Sentence**

> After years of research, the team finally identified the gene responsible for the rare disorder **:** a breakthrough that would transform treatment protocols worldwide.

A) NO CHANGE
B) disorder, a breakthrough
C) disorder; a breakthrough
D) disorder—a breakthrough

**Strategic Analysis:**

- "After years of research, the team finally identified the gene responsible for the rare disorder" → IC
- "a breakthrough that would transform treatment protocols worldwide" → Noun phrase (not a complete sentence — no main verb for "a breakthrough")

A colon can introduce a noun phrase that explains the preceding clause. A dash can also add information at the end of a sentence, typically for emphasis.

Both A (colon) and D (dash) are grammatically acceptable. The question is which is more appropriate.

The colon is more conventional for introducing an explanation. The dash adds dramatic emphasis. On the ACT, when both are grammatically correct, the colon is typically preferred for explanatory content at the end of a sentence, while the dash is preferred for informal or emphatic additions.

However, "a breakthrough that would transform treatment protocols worldwide" is a significant, emphatic statement. The dash adds appropriate weight.

**Answer: D**

**Key Principle:** Dashes at the end of a sentence add emphasis or dramatic effect. Colons at the end introduce explanations. Both are grammatically correct; the choice depends on the desired tone.

---

**Problem 24: Interchangeability of Dashes, Commas, and Parentheses**

> The novel's protagonist—**a disillusioned war veteran struggling to reintegrate into civilian life**—embarks on a journey of self-discovery.

The writer would like to change the dashes to commas. Would this change improve the sentence?

A) Yes, because commas are always preferred over dashes in formal writing.
B) Yes, because the information is not important enough to warrant emphasis.
C) No, because the dashes correctly set off a nonessential clause.
D) No, because the change would not alter the grammatical correctness of the sentence.

**Strategic Analysis:**

The dashes set off a nonessential MCC. Changing them to commas would still be grammatically correct — dashes, commas, and parentheses are interchangeable for MCCs. The only difference is emphasis level.

The question asks whether the change would "improve" the sentence. Since both are grammatically correct, the question is really about whether commas are "better."

- **A)** "Commas are always preferred" — this is false. Dashes are equally valid. Wrong.
- **B)** "Not important enough to warrant emphasis" — this is subjective and not a grammatical reason. Wrong.
- **C)** "Dashes correctly set off a nonessential clause" — true, but this doesn't explain why changing to commas would be wrong.
- **D)** "The change would not alter the grammatical correctness" — this is the key insight. Since both are correct, the change doesn't "improve" the sentence; it merely changes emphasis. The question implies that "improve" means "make more correct," and since both are correct, no improvement is needed.

**Answer: D**

---

**Problem 25: Dash vs. Colon at Mid-Sentence**

> One factor determines the outcome of the experiment **:** the temperature at which the reaction occurs.

A) NO CHANGE
B) experiment, the temperature
C) experiment—the temperature
D) experiment; the temperature

**Strategic Analysis:**

- "One factor determines the outcome of the experiment" → IC
- "the temperature at which the reaction occurs" → Noun phrase (not a complete sentence)

A colon can introduce a noun phrase after a complete sentence. A dash can also add information at the end of a sentence.

Both A and C are grammatically acceptable. The colon is more conventional for introducing a specific explanation of "one factor." The dash adds emphasis.

On the ACT, the colon is preferred when the second part specifically identifies or explains what was mentioned in the first part.

**Answer: A**

---

#### PROBLEM SET 5: APOSTROPHE MASTERY (5 Problems)

---

**Problem 26: Its vs. It's**

> The company announced **it's** new policy on remote work, effective immediately.

A) NO CHANGE
B) its
C) its'
D) its's

**Strategic Analysis:**

- "It's" = contraction of "it is" or "it has"
- "Its" = possessive pronoun (belonging to it)

In this sentence, we need the possessive form: "its new policy" = the new policy belonging to it (the company).

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "it's" = "it is" — "The company announced it is new policy" makes no sense. Wrong.
- **B)** "its" — possessive. Correct.
- **C)** "its'" — this form does not exist in English. Wrong.
- **D)** "its's" — this form does not exist. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

**Key Principle:** The ACT tests "its" vs. "it's" frequently. Remember: possessive pronouns (his, hers, its, ours, yours, theirs, whose) NEVER have apostrophes. The apostrophe in "it's" signals a contraction, not possession.

---

**Problem 27: Possessive with a Singular Noun**

> **James**'s contributions to the field of quantum mechanics were unparalleled.

A) NO CHANGE
B) James'
C) Jame's
D) Jameses'

**Strategic Analysis:**

For singular nouns (including those ending in "s"), the ACT accepts **'s** as the possessive form. "James's" is correct.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "James's" — correct for a singular noun.
- **B)** "James'" — some style guides accept this for singular proper nouns ending in s, but the ACT prefers 's for all singular nouns.
- **C)** "Jame's" — misspelling of the name. Wrong.
- **D)** "Jameses'" — this would be the possessive of a plural "Jameses," which doesn't exist. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 28: Plural Possessive**

> The **childrens**' toys were scattered across the living room floor.

A) NO CHANGE
B) children's
C) childrens's
D) childrens'

**Strategic Analysis:**

"Children" is an irregular plural (not "childrens"). The possessive of "children" is "children's" (plural not ending in s → add 's).

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "childrens'" — "childrens" is not a word. Wrong.
- **B)** "children's" — correct possessive of the irregular plural "children."
- **C)** "childrens's" — double error. Wrong.
- **D)** "childrens'" — "childrens" is not a word. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 29: Pronoun Possessives**

> The decision was **their's** to make, not ours.

A) NO CHANGE
B) theirs
C) their
D) there's

**Strategic Analysis:**

Possessive pronouns never have apostrophes: his, hers, its, ours, yours, theirs, whose.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "their's" — apostrophe is wrong. Wrong.
- **B)** "theirs" — correct possessive pronoun.
- **C)** "their" — this is a possessive adjective (used before a noun: "their decision"), not a standalone possessive pronoun. Wrong.
- **D)** "there's" = "there is" — makes no sense here. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 30: Contraction vs. Possessive in Context**

> **Who's** responsibility is it to ensure the laboratory meets safety standards?

A) NO CHANGE
B) Whose
C) Whom
D) Who

**Strategic Analysis:**

- "Who's" = "who is" or "who has"
- "Whose" = possessive of "who"

The sentence asks about possession: whose responsibility? "Whose responsibility is it..." is correct.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "Who's" = "who is" — "Who is responsibility is it..." makes no sense. Wrong.
- **B)** "Whose" — possessive. Correct.
- **C)** "Whom" — object pronoun, cannot show possession. Wrong.
- **D)** "Who" — subject pronoun, cannot show possession. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

### Section A.2: Subject-Verb Agreement Mastery

---

#### PROBLEM SET 6: SUBJECT-VERB AGREEMENT (10 Problems)

---

**Problem 31: Subject Separated from Verb by a Prepositional Phrase**

> The collection of rare manuscripts **are** housed in the university's special collections library.

A) NO CHANGE
B) is
C) were
D) have been

**Strategic Analysis:**

Apply the SVA process:

1. Cross out prepositional phrases: "of rare manuscripts" and "in the university's special collections library"
2. Subject: "The collection" — singular
3. Verb must be singular: "is"

The trap: "manuscripts" is plural and sits right next to the verb, tempting you to choose "are." But "manuscripts" is inside a prepositional phrase and CANNOT be the subject.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "are" — plural verb with singular subject. Wrong.
- **B)** "is" — singular. Correct.
- **C)** "were" — plural past tense. Wrong.
- **D)** "have been" — plural. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 32: "Each" as Subject**

> Each of the students in the advanced calculus class **have** completed the assignment.

A) NO CHANGE
B) has
C) are
D) were

**Strategic Analysis:**

"Each" is ALWAYS singular, regardless of what follows. "Each of the students" → "Each" is the subject → singular verb.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "have" — plural. Wrong.
- **B)** "has" — singular. Correct.
- **C)** "are" — plural. Wrong.
- **D)** "were" — plural. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 33: "There" Construction**

> There **is** several reasons why the proposal was rejected.

A) NO CHANGE
B) are
C) was
D) has been

**Strategic Analysis:**

When a sentence begins with "There," the subject comes AFTER the verb. Cross out everything before the verb to find the subject:

"There **are** several reasons why the proposal was rejected."

Subject: "several reasons" — plural. Verb must be plural.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "is" — singular with plural subject. Wrong.
- **B)** "are" — plural. Correct.
- **C)** "was" — singular past. Wrong.
- **D)** "has been" — singular. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 34: Compound Subject with "And"**

> The director and the producer **has** agreed to revise the script.

A) NO CHANGE
B) have
C) is
D) was

**Strategic Analysis:**

Subjects joined by "and" are compound and take a plural verb. "The director and the producer" = plural.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "has" — singular. Wrong.
- **B)** "have" — plural. Correct.
- **C)** "is" — singular. Wrong.
- **D)** "was" — singular. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 35: "As Well As" Does Not Create a Compound Subject**

> The CEO, as well as the board members, **are** attending the conference.

A) NO CHANGE
B) is
C) have been
D) were

**Strategic Analysis:**

Phrases like "as well as," "along with," "in addition to," "together with," and "accompanied by" do NOT create compound subjects. The subject is what comes BEFORE these phrases.

Subject: "The CEO" — singular. The phrase "as well as the board members" is parenthetical and does not affect agreement.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "are" — plural. Wrong.
- **B)** "is" — singular. Correct.
- **C)** "have been" — plural. Wrong.
- **D)** "were" — plural. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 36: "A Number Of" vs. "The Number Of"**

> The number of applicants for the scholarship **have** increased significantly this year.

A) NO CHANGE
B) has
C) are
D) were

**Strategic Analysis:**

- "A number of" = plural (meaning "many")
- "The number of" = singular (referring to the numerical value itself)

Here: "The number of applicants" — "number" is the subject, and it's singular.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "have" — plural. Wrong.
- **B)** "has" — singular. Correct.
- **C)** "are" — plural. Wrong.
- **D)** "were" — plural. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 37: Relative Clause Interruption**

> The students who **studies** diligently tend to perform well on standardized tests.

A) NO CHANGE
B) study
C) has studied
D) was studying

**Strategic Analysis:**

The relative clause "who studies diligently" modifies "The students" (plural). The verb in the relative clause must agree with its antecedent ("students"), not with "who" in isolation.

"Students who study" — "study" must be plural to agree with "students."

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "studies" — singular. Wrong.
- **B)** "study" — plural. Correct.
- **C)** "has studied" — singular. Wrong.
- **D)** "was studying" — singular. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 38: Gerund as Subject**

> **Analyzing complex datasets** require a sophisticated understanding of statistical methods.

A) NO CHANGE
B) requires
C) are requiring
D) have required

**Strategic Analysis:**

"-ing" words functioning as nouns (gerunds) are singular subjects. "Analyzing complex datasets" is a gerund phrase acting as the subject → singular.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "require" — plural. Wrong.
- **B)** "requires" — singular. Correct.
- **C)** "are requiring" — plural. Wrong.
- **D)** "have required" — plural. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 39: Inverted Sentence Structure**

> Among the artifacts **was** a bronze ceremonial dagger dating back to the third century BCE.

A) NO CHANGE
B) were
C) is
D) has been

**Strategic Analysis:**

This is an inverted sentence. The normal order would be: "A bronze ceremonial dagger dating back to the third century BCE was among the artifacts."

Subject: "a bronze ceremonial dagger" — singular. The verb must be singular.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "was" — singular. Correct.
- **B)** "were" — plural. Wrong.
- **C)** "is" — singular present, but the context (dating back to the third century BCE) suggests past tense. Wrong.
- **D)** "has been" — present perfect, doesn't fit the context. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 40: "Every" as Subject Modifier**

> Every participant in the clinical trials **receive** a comprehensive health assessment.

A) NO CHANGE
B) receives
C) are receiving
D) have received

**Strategic Analysis:**

"Every" is ALWAYS singular. "Every participant" → singular subject → singular verb.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "receive" — plural. Wrong.
- **B)** "receives" — singular. Correct.
- **C)** "are receiving" — plural. Wrong.
- **D)** "have received" — plural. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

### Section A.3: Modifier Mastery

---

#### PROBLEM SET 7: MODIFIERS (10 Problems)

---

**Problem 41: Dangling Modifier (Introductory)**

> **Walking through the forest**, the autumn leaves created a vibrant tapestry of color.

A) NO CHANGE
B) Walking through the forest, the autumn leaves were creating
C) As I walked through the forest, the autumn leaves created
D) Walking through the forest, I saw the autumn leaves creating

**Strategic Analysis:**

The introductory clause "Walking through the forest" describes an action. The subject that follows must be the person/thing performing that action.

- "Walking through the forest, the autumn leaves created..." → The leaves were not walking. This is a **dangling modifier**.

The subject must be changed to someone who can walk:
- **D)** "Walking through the forest, I saw the autumn leaves creating..." → "I" can walk. Correct.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Dangling modifier. Wrong.
- **B)** Still has the leaves as the subject. Wrong.
- **C)** "As I walked through the forest, the autumn leaves created" — this is grammatically correct! The "As I walked" clause has "I" as its subject, and the main clause has "the autumn leaves" as its subject. This is a valid structure.

Wait — both C and D are grammatically correct. Which is better?

C uses a dependent clause ("As I walked") with a separate main clause. D uses an introductory participial phrase where "I" is the subject of both the walking and the seeing.

Both are acceptable. However, D more directly fixes the modifier error by making "I" the subject of the main clause, which is the standard way to fix dangling modifiers. C changes the structure more significantly.

On the ACT, when both fix the error, prefer the answer that most directly addresses the original problem while maintaining the original meaning and structure as much as possible.

**Answer: D**

---

**Problem 42: Misplaced Modifier**

> The professor explained the theory **to the students using vivid diagrams**.

A) NO CHANGE
B) to the students, using vivid diagrams.
C) using vivid diagrams to the students.
D) to the students; using vivid diagrams.

**Strategic Analysis:**

The modifier "using vivid diagrams" should be placed as close as possible to the word it modifies. In the original, it's unclear whether the students were using vivid diagrams or the professor was.

The intended meaning is that the professor used vivid diagrams to explain the theory.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Ambiguous — who is using the diagrams? Wrong.
- **B)** Comma before "using" — this still leaves ambiguity about who is using the diagrams.
- **C)** "using vivid diagrams to the students" — the participial phrase "using vivid diagrams" is now at the beginning of the phrase, clearly modifying "the professor" (the subject of the main clause). Correct.
- **D)** Semicolon — creates an awkward break and doesn't resolve the ambiguity.

**Answer: C**

---

**Problem 43: Introductory Comma Clause with Correct Subject**

> **Having studied for weeks**, the exam felt manageable to the well-prepared student.

A) NO CHANGE
B) Having studied for weeks, the well-prepared student found the exam manageable.
C) The exam, having studied for weeks, felt manageable to the well-prepared student.
D) Having studied for weeks, the exam was felt manageable by the well-prepared student.

**Strategic Analysis:**

"Having studied for weeks" is an introductory participial phrase. The subject that follows must be the one who studied.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "the exam" cannot study. Dangling modifier. Wrong.
- **B)** "the well-prepared student" can study. Correct.
- **C)** The participial phrase is inserted mid-sentence, and "the exam" is still the subject. Wrong.
- **D)** "the exam" cannot study. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 44: Ending Comma Clause**

> The scientist presented her findings to the committee, **hoping to secure additional funding for her research**.

A) NO CHANGE
B) hoped to secure additional funding for her research.
C) and hoping to secure additional funding for her research.
D) to hope to secure additional funding for her research.

**Strategic Analysis:**

The ending comma clause "hoping to secure additional funding for her research" is an "-ing" participial phrase that modifies the subject of the main clause ("the scientist"). It describes the scientist's purpose or state of mind while presenting.

The comma is critical here. Without it, the sentence would be grammatically incorrect or ambiguous.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Comma + "-ing" phrase modifying the subject. Correct.
- **B)** "hoped" — this creates a compound verb ("presented... and hoped"), but without "and," it's a verb tense error. Wrong.
- **C)** "and hoping" — "and" + "-ing" is not parallel with "presented." Wrong.
- **D)** "to hope" — awkward and ungrammatical in this context. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 45: Middle Comma Clause (Appositive)**

> The novel, **a sprawling epic that spans three generations**, won the Pulitzer Prize.

A) NO CHANGE
B) a sprawling epic, that spans three generations,
C) a sprawling epic that spans three generations;
D) a sprawling epic that spans three generations

**Strategic Analysis:**

"a sprawling epic that spans three generations" is an appositive renaming "The novel." It is nonessential (the novel is already identified as "The novel"), so it must be set off with commas on both sides.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Commas on both sides. Correct.
- **B)** Comma before "that" — "that" introduces a restrictive clause and should not be preceded by a comma. Wrong.
- **C)** Semicolon — cannot be used to set off an appositive. Wrong.
- **D)** No commas — the appositive is not set off. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 46: Dangling Modifier with "After"**

> **After completing the marathon**, the medal felt like a tremendous achievement.

A) NO CHANGE
B) After completing the marathon, the medal was felt
C) After I completed the marathon, the medal felt
D) After completing the marathon, I felt that the medal was

**Strategic Analysis:**

"After completing the marathon" — who completed the marathon? The medal cannot complete a marathon.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Dangling modifier. Wrong.
- **B)** "the medal" cannot complete a marathon. Wrong.
- **C)** "After I completed the marathon, the medal felt" — "I" completed the marathon (correct), but "the medal felt" is awkward (medals don't feel). This is grammatically acceptable but semantically odd.
- **D)** "After completing the marathon, I felt that the medal was" — "I" completed the marathon and "I" felt. Correct and natural.

**Answer: D**

---

**Problem 47: Participial Phrase at the Beginning**

> **Exhausted from the long journey**, the hotel bed was a welcome sight to the travelers.

A) NO CHANGE
B) Exhausted from the long journey, the travelers found the hotel bed
C) The hotel bed, exhausted from the long journey, was
D) Exhausted from the long journey; the hotel bed was

**Strategic Analysis:**

"Exhausted from the long journey" must modify someone who was exhausted. The hotel bed was not exhausted.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Dangling modifier. Wrong.
- **B)** "the travelers" were exhausted. Correct.
- **C)** "the hotel bed" was exhausted. Wrong.
- **D)** Semicolon doesn't fix the dangling modifier. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 48: Modifier Placement for Clarity**

> The chef prepared the meal **with great care that was served to the guests**.

A) NO CHANGE
B) The chef prepared the meal that was served to the guests with great care.
C) With great care, the chef prepared the meal that was served to the guests.
D) The chef prepared with great care the meal that was served to the guests.

**Strategic Analysis:**

The original is ambiguous: was the meal served with great care, or was the preparation done with great care?

The intended meaning is that the chef prepared the meal with great care.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Ambiguous. Wrong.
- **B)** "the meal that was served to the guests with great care" — still ambiguous. The "with great care" could modify "served." Wrong.
- **C)** "With great care" at the beginning clearly modifies "prepared." The relative clause "that was served to the guests" clearly modifies "the meal." Correct.
- **D)** "prepared with great care the meal" — awkward word order. Wrong.

**Answer: C**

---

**Problem 49: "Which" Clause Placement**

> The report was filed late, **which disappointed the client**.

A) NO CHANGE
B) which the client was disappointed by.
C) a fact which disappointed the client.
D) , disappointing the client.

**Strategic Analysis:**

The "which" clause "which disappointed the client" should clearly refer to a specific noun or idea. In the original, "which" seems to refer to the entire idea of the report being filed late, which is acceptable but could be clearer.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "which" refers to the entire preceding clause. This is acceptable but slightly informal.
- **B)** Passive and awkward. Wrong.
- **C)** "a fact which" — adds an unnecessary noun. Wordy.
- **D)** ", disappointing the client" — a participial phrase that clearly modifies the entire preceding action. Concise and correct.

**Answer: D**

---

**Problem 50: Squinting Modifier**

> The students who **practice regularly improve** their scores significantly.

A) NO CHANGE
B. practice regularly, improve
C. practice regularly improving
D. practice regularly, and improve

**Strategic Analysis:**

The original is ambiguous: does "regularly" modify "practice" or "improve"? It's a squinting modifier — it could go either way.

The intended meaning is that students who practice regularly (as a habit) improve their scores.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Ambiguous. Wrong.
- **B)** "practice regularly, improve" — the comma separates the clauses, making it clear that "regularly" modifies "practice." Correct.
- **C)** "practice regularly improving" — awkward and ungrammatical. Wrong.
- **D)** "practice regularly, and improve" — the "and" creates an unnecessary compound verb. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

### Section A.4: Pronoun Mastery

---

#### PROBLEM SET 8: PRONOUNS (8 Problems)

---

**Problem 51: Who vs. Whom**

> The scientist **who** the committee nominated for the award has published over fifty papers.

A) NO CHANGE
B) whom
C) whose
D) which

**Strategic Analysis:**

Test: Replace with "he" or "him."
- "The committee nominated he" → wrong
- "The committee nominated him" → correct

Since "him" works, use "whom."

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "who" — subject pronoun, but this is an object position. Wrong.
- **B)** "whom" — object pronoun. Correct.
- **C)** "whose" — possessive. Wrong.
- **D)** "which" — used for things, not people. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 52: Who vs. Whom in a Question**

> **Who** did you say is responsible for the project?

A) NO CHANGE
B) Whom
C) Whomever
D) Whose

**Strategic Analysis:**

In the clause "___ is responsible for the project," the pronoun is the SUBJECT of "is." Test:
- "He is responsible" → correct → use "who"
- "Him is responsible" → wrong

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "who" — subject pronoun. Correct.
- **B)** "whom" — object pronoun. Wrong.
- **C)** "whomever" — object form. Wrong.
- **D)** "whose" — possessive. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 53: Pronoun-Antecedent Agreement**

> Every student must submit **their** assignment by Friday.

A) NO CHANGE
B) his or her
C) its
D) our

**Strategic Analysis:**

"Every student" is singular. The pronoun must be singular. The ACT does NOT accept "they/their" as a gender-neutral singular pronoun.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "their" — plural with singular antecedent. Wrong on the ACT.
- **B)** "his or her" — singular. Correct.
- **C)** "its" — used for things, not people. Wrong.
- **D)** "our" — first person, doesn't match "every student." Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 54: Unclear Pronoun Reference**

> When the director spoke with the producer, **he** was visibly upset.

A) NO CHANGE
B) the director was visibly upset.
C) he, the director, was visibly upset.
D) he was upset, being visibly so.

**Strategic Analysis:**

"He" is ambiguous — does it refer to the director or the producer? The pronoun has no clear antecedent.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Ambiguous. Wrong.
- **B)** "the director" — removes ambiguity. Correct.
- **C)** "he, the director" — still uses "he" which is unnecessary. The appositive "the director" clarifies, but the sentence is wordy.
- **D)** Still uses "he" and adds unnecessary words. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 55: Pronoun Case in Compound**

> The award was given to **my colleague and I** for our groundbreaking research.

A) NO CHANGE
B) my colleague and me
C) I and my colleague
D) me and my colleague

**Strategic Analysis:**

Test by removing the other person: "The award was given to I" → wrong. "The award was given to me" → correct.

Use the objective case "me" because the pronoun is the object of the preposition "to."

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "I" — subjective case in an objective position. Wrong.
- **B)** "my colleague and me" — objective case. Correct.
- **C)** "I" — subjective case. Wrong.
- **D)** "me and my colleague" — grammatically correct but impolite (put yourself last). The ACT prefers "my colleague and me."

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 56: "Who" in a Relative Clause**

> The researchers, **who** have been studying the phenomenon for decades, published their findings.

A) NO CHANGE
B) whom
C) which
D) that

**Strategic Analysis:**

The relative clause "who have been studying the phenomenon for decades" modifies "The researchers" (people). "Who" is the subject of "have been studying."

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "who" — subject pronoun for people. Correct.
- **B)** "whom" — object pronoun. Wrong.
- **C)** "which" — for things, not people. Wrong.
- **D)** "that" — not used in nonrestrictive clauses (with commas). Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 57: Pronoun Consistency**

> If one studies diligently, **you** will likely succeed.

A) NO CHANGE
B) they
C) one
D) we

**Strategic Analysis:**

The sentence begins with "one" (third person, formal). The pronoun must be consistent.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "you" — shifts from "one" to "you." Inconsistent. Wrong.
- **B)** "they" — shifts from singular "one" to plural "they." Wrong.
- **C)** "one" — consistent with the opening "one." Correct.
- **D)** "we" — shifts from "one" to "we." Wrong.

**Answer: C**

---

**Problem 58: "Whose" for Possession**

> The architect **whose** designs won the international competition will lead the new project.

A) NO CHANGE
B) who's
C) whom
D) which

**Strategic Analysis:**

"Whose" shows possession — the designs belong to the architect.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "whose" — possessive. Correct.
- **B)** "who's" = "who is" — doesn't show possession. Wrong.
- **C)** "whom" — object pronoun, no possession. Wrong.
- **D)** "which" — for things, not people. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

### Section A.5: Verb Tense Mastery

---

#### PROBLEM SET 9: VERB TENSES (8 Problems)

---

**Problem 59: Past Perfect**

> By the time the rescue team arrived, the hikers **waited** for over twelve hours.

A) NO CHANGE
B) had waited
C) have waited
D) were waiting

**Strategic Analysis:**

Two past actions:
1. The hikers waited (first)
2. The rescue team arrived (second)

The action that happened FIRST (waiting) requires past perfect ("had waited") because it occurred before another past action (arrived).

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "waited" — simple past, doesn't show the sequence. Wrong.
- **B)** "had waited" — past perfect. Correct.
- **C)** "have waited" — present perfect, doesn't fit the past context. Wrong.
- **D)** "were waiting" — past continuous, doesn't show completion before the arrival. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 60: Present Perfect with "Since"**

> She **has been** a professor at the university since 2010.

A) NO CHANGE
B) was
C) had been
D) is

**Strategic Analysis:**

"Since 2010" indicates an action that started in the past and continues to the present. This requires present perfect ("has been").

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "has been" — present perfect. Correct.
- **B)** "was" — simple past, implies she is no longer a professor. Wrong.
- **C)** "had been" — past perfect, requires a past reference point. Wrong.
- **D)** "is" — simple present, doesn't convey the duration since 2010. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 61: Tense Consistency**

> The author wrote the novel in 1995, and it **remains** a classic of modern literature.

A) NO CHANGE
B) remained
C) has remained
D) will remain

**Strategic Analysis:**

The first verb "wrote" is past tense (the writing happened in 1995). The second verb describes the novel's current status — it STILL remains a classic. This requires present tense.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "remains" — simple present, correctly indicates current status. Correct.
- **B)** "remained" — past tense, implies it is no longer a classic. Wrong.
- **C)** "has remained" — present perfect, also acceptable (emphasizes continuity from past to present). But "remains" is more direct.
- **D)** "will remain" — future tense, changes the meaning. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 62: "Would" vs. "Will"**

> If the experiment succeeds, it **will** revolutionize the field.

A) NO CHANGE
B) would
C) could
D) can

**Strategic Analysis:**

This is a **first conditional** (real/possible condition). Structure: If + present, will + base verb.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "will" — correct for a real conditional. Correct.
- **B)** "would" — used in second conditionals (unreal/hypothetical). Wrong.
- **C)** "could" — possible but less definitive than "will." The sentence implies certainty.
- **D)** "can" — present tense, doesn't match the future consequence. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 63: Past Perfect with Reference Point**

> The historian discovered that the document **had been forged** centuries earlier.

A) NO CHANGE
B) was forged
C) has been forged
D) is forged

**Strategic Analysis:**

Two past actions:
1. The document was forged (first, centuries earlier)
2. The historian discovered (second)

The earlier action requires past perfect.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "had been forged" — past perfect passive. Correct.
- **B)** "was forged" — simple past, doesn't show the sequence. Wrong.
- **C)** "has been forged" — present perfect, doesn't fit. Wrong.
- **D)** "is forged" — present tense, wrong time frame. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 64: Present Perfect with "For"**

> The company **has operated** in the region for over fifty years.

A) NO CHANGE
B) operated
C) had operated
D) was operating

**Strategic Analysis:**

"For over fifty years" with present relevance requires present perfect.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "has operated" — present perfect. Correct.
- **B)** "operated" — simple past, implies the company no longer operates there. Wrong.
- **C)** "had operated" — past perfect, needs a past reference point. Wrong.
- **D)** "was operating" — past continuous, doesn't convey duration. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 65: Sequence of Tenses**

> The professor explained that water **boils** at 100 degrees Celsius.

A) NO CHANGE
B) boiled
C) had boiled
D) would boil

**Strategic Analysis:**

This is a **universal truth** (scientific fact). Even though the main verb "explained" is past tense, universal truths remain in present tense.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "boils" — present tense for universal truth. Correct.
- **B)** "boiled" — past tense, implies water no longer boils at 100°C. Wrong.
- **C)** "had boiled" — past perfect, wrong. Wrong.
- **D)** "would boil" — conditional, wrong. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 66: Past Perfect Necessity**

> She **already left** when I called her.

A) NO CHANGE
B) has already left
C) had already left
D) was already leaving

**Strategic Analysis:**

Two past actions:
1. She left (first)
2. I called (second)

The earlier action requires past perfect.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "already left" — simple past, doesn't show sequence. Wrong.
- **B)** "has already left" — present perfect, doesn't fit past context. Wrong.
- **C)** "had already left" — past perfect. Correct.
- **D)** "was already leaving" — past continuous, doesn't show completion. Wrong.

**Answer: C**

---

### Section A.6: Parallel Structure Mastery

---

#### PROBLEM SET 10: PARALLELISM (6 Problems)

---

**Problem 67: Parallel Items in a List**

> The internship program offers students the opportunity to gain practical experience, develop professional networks, **and building** leadership skills.

A) NO CHANGE
B) to build leadership skills.
C) building leadership skills.
D) leadership skills are built.

**Strategic Analysis:**

The list has three items:
1. to gain practical experience
2. develop professional networks
3. and building leadership skills

Items 1 and 2 use the infinitive/base form. Item 3 uses "-ing." This breaks parallelism.

The structure should be: "to gain..., [to] develop..., and [to] build..."

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "building" — not parallel. Wrong.
- **B)** "to build" — parallel with "to gain" and "develop" (the "to" can be distributed). Correct.
- **C)** "building" — not parallel. Wrong.
- **D)** Changes the structure entirely. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 68: Parallel Structure with Correlative Conjunctions**

> The new policy is **both** innovative **and** it challenges traditional assumptions.

A) NO CHANGE
B) both innovative and challenging
C) innovative and it challenges
D) innovative and also challenges

**Strategic Analysis:**

"Both... and..." requires parallel structure. After "both" we have "innovative" (adjective). After "and" we need another adjective.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "it challenges traditional assumptions" — a clause, not parallel with "innovative." Wrong.
- **B)** "innovative and challenging" — two adjectives. Parallel. Correct.
- **C)** Removes "both" but still has a clause after "and." Wrong.
- **D)** "also" is redundant with "and." Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 69: Parallelism with "Not Only... But Also"**

> The film is **not only** visually stunning **but** it also features a compelling narrative.

A) NO CHANGE
B) not only visually stunning but also features
C) not only visually stunning but also featuring
D) visually stunning not only but also

**Strategic Analysis:**

"Not only... but also" requires parallel structure. After "not only" we have "visually stunning" (adjective phrase). After "but also" we need a parallel adjective phrase.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "it also features a compelling narrative" — a clause, not parallel. Wrong.
- **B)** "but also features" — a verb phrase, not parallel with "visually stunning." Wrong.
- **C)** "but also featuring" — a participial phrase, still not parallel with "visually stunning." Hmm.

Wait — let me reconsider. The intended parallel structure might be:
- "not only visually stunning but also narratively compelling"

But none of the options give us that. Let me re-examine:

Actually, the most natural reading is that the sentence should be:
- "The film is not only visually stunning but also features a compelling narrative."

But this isn't strictly parallel. The ACT sometimes accepts this construction when the meaning is clear.

Alternatively, the sentence could be:
- "The film not only is visually stunning but also features a compelling narrative."

But this isn't an option either.

Given the options, **B** is the most natural and commonly accepted construction, even if it's not perfectly parallel in the strictest sense.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 70: Parallelism in Comparisons**

> The CEO's salary is higher than **the company's lowest-paid workers**.

A) NO CHANGE
B) the company's lowest-paid workers' salary.
C) that of the company's lowest-paid workers.
D) those of the company's lowest-paid workers.

**Strategic Analysis:**

We're comparing the CEO's salary to the workers' salaries. The comparison must be between like things: salary vs. salary (or salaries).

- **A) NO CHANGE:** Compares salary to workers (not parallel). Wrong.
- **B)** "workers' salary" — implies all workers share one salary. Awkward.
- **C)** "that of the company's lowest-paid workers" — "that" refers to "salary" (singular). Correct comparison: CEO's salary vs. the salary of the workers. Correct.
- **D)** "those" — plural, but "salary" is singular. Wrong.

**Answer: C**

---

**Problem 71: Parallel Structure with Verbs**

> The committee reviewed the proposal, **discussed its implications, and a vote was taken**.

A) NO CHANGE
B) discussed its implications, and voted on it.
C) discussing its implications, and voted.
D) discussed its implications; and a vote was taken.

**Strategic Analysis:**

The list should have three parallel verbs:
1. reviewed
2. discussed
3. [should be a verb in the same form]

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "a vote was taken" — passive voice, not parallel with active verbs. Wrong.
- **B)** "voted on it" — active verb, parallel with "reviewed" and "discussed." Correct.
- **C)** "discussing" — breaks parallelism. Wrong.
- **D)** Semicolon doesn't fix the parallelism issue. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 72: Parallelism with "Rather Than"**

> The author chose to focus on character development **rather than plot** advancement.

A) NO CHANGE
B) rather than advancing the plot.
C) rather than to advance the plot.
D) rather than the plot.

**Strategic Analysis:**

"Rather than" requires parallel structure. Before "rather than" we have "to focus on character development" (infinitive phrase). After "rather than" we need a parallel structure.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "plot advancement" — noun phrase, not parallel with "to focus on character development." Wrong.
- **B)** "advancing the plot" — gerund phrase, not parallel with infinitive. Wrong.
- **C)** "to advance the plot" — infinitive, parallel with "to focus." Correct.
- **D)** "the plot" — noun, not parallel. Wrong.

**Answer: C**

---

## PART B: PRODUCTION OF WRITING — RHETORIC QUESTIONS

### Section B.1: Transitions

---

#### PROBLEM SET 11: TRANSITION WORDS (10 Problems)

---

**Problem 73: Contrast Transition**

> The experiment was designed to test the hypothesis. **Furthermore**, the results contradicted the researchers' expectations.

A) NO CHANGE
B) However
C) Therefore
D) Similarly

**Strategic Analysis:**

The first sentence says the experiment was designed to test a hypothesis. The second sentence says the results CONTRADICTED expectations. This is a CONTRAST relationship — the results went against what was expected.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "Furthermore" — addition, not contrast. Wrong.
- **B)** "However" — contrast. Correct.
- **C)** "Therefore" — cause and effect. Wrong.
- **D)** "Similarly" — similarity. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 74: Cause and Effect Transition**

> The company invested heavily in research and development. **Nevertheless**, it launched a groundbreaking product within two years.

A) NO CHANGE
B) Consequently
C) On the other hand
D) Meanwhile

**Strategic Analysis:**

Investing in R&D (cause) led to launching a groundbreaking product (effect). This is a CAUSE AND EFFECT relationship.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "Nevertheless" — contrast/concession. Wrong.
- **B)** "Consequently" — cause and effect. Correct.
- **C)** "On the other hand" — contrast. Wrong.
- **D)** "Meanwhile" — time/sequence. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 75: Addition Transition**

> The novel explores themes of identity and belonging. **In fact**, it also examines the tension between tradition and modernity.

A) NO CHANGE
B) In contrast
C) Moreover
D) Therefore

**Strategic Analysis:**

The first sentence mentions themes of identity and belonging. The second sentence adds ANOTHER theme (tradition vs. modernity). This is an ADDITION relationship.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "In fact" — illustration/emphasis. This could work if the second sentence is emphasizing or illustrating the first, but "also" in the second sentence signals addition.
- **B)** "In contrast" — contrast. Wrong.
- **C)** "Moreover" — addition. Correct.
- **D)** "Therefore" — cause and effect. Wrong.

**Answer: C**

---

**Problem 76: Illustration Transition**

> The city has implemented several innovative sustainability initiatives. **For example**, it has installed solar panels on all municipal buildings.

A) NO CHANGE
B) Nevertheless
C) In summary
D) Conversely

**Strategic Analysis:**

The first sentence makes a general claim (sustainability initiatives). The second sentence provides a SPECIFIC EXAMPLE. This is an ILLUSTRATION relationship.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "For example" — illustration. Correct.
- **B)** "Nevertheless" — contrast. Wrong.
- **C)** "In summary" — conclusion. Wrong.
- **D)** "Conversely" — contrast. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 77: Sequence Transition**

> The team conducted extensive market research. **Subsequently**, they developed a comprehensive marketing strategy.

A) NO CHANGE
B) Nevertheless
C) For instance
D) Similarly

**Strategic Analysis:**

Market research happened FIRST, then the marketing strategy was developed. This is a SEQUENCE relationship.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "Subsequently" — sequence/order. Correct.
- **B)** "Nevertheless" — contrast. Wrong.
- **C)** "For instance" — illustration. Wrong.
- **D)** "Similarly" — similarity. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 78: Concession Transition**

> **Granted**, the initial costs of the project are high, but the long-term benefits far outweigh them.

A) NO CHANGE
B) Furthermore
C) Therefore
D) Meanwhile

**Strategic Analysis:**

The sentence concedes a point (high initial costs) to make a more important point (long-term benefits outweigh them). This is a CONCESSION relationship.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "Granted" — concession. Correct.
- **B)** "Furthermore" — addition. Wrong.
- **C)** "Therefore" — cause and effect. Wrong.
- **D)** "Meanwhile" — time. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 79: Similarity Transition**

> The first study found a strong correlation between exercise and mental health. **Similarly**, the second study confirmed these findings.

A) NO CHANGE
B) However
C) Consequently
D) In contrast

**Strategic Analysis:**

Both studies found similar results. This is a SIMILARITY relationship.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "Similarly" — similarity. Correct.
- **B)** "However" — contrast. Wrong.
- **C)** "Consequently" — cause and effect. Wrong.
- **D)** "In contrast" — contrast. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 80: Conclusion Transition**

> The data clearly supports the hypothesis. **In summary**, the experiment was a success.

A) NO CHANGE
B) Nevertheless
C) For example
D) Meanwhile

**Strategic Analysis:**

The second sentence provides a CONCLUSION based on the first sentence's evidence.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "In summary" — conclusion. Correct.
- **B)** "Nevertheless" — contrast. Wrong.
- **C)** "For example" — illustration. Wrong.
- **D)** "Meanwhile" — time. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 81: Contrast with "Whereas"**

> **Whereas** the northern region experienced heavy rainfall, the southern region suffered from drought.

A) NO CHANGE
B) Because
C) Therefore
D) Moreover

**Strategic Analysis:**

Two contrasting situations: heavy rainfall in the north vs. drought in the south. "Whereas" is a contrast transition.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "Whereas" — contrast. Correct.
- **B)** "Because" — cause and effect. Wrong.
- **C)** "Therefore" — cause and effect. Wrong.
- **D)** "Moreover" — addition. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 82: Transition with "Indeed"**

> The new policy has been effective. **Indeed**, employee productivity has increased by 20%.

A) NO CHANGE
B) However
C) Conversely
D) Meanwhile

**Strategic Analysis:**

The second sentence provides EVIDENCE that EMPHASIZES and SUPPORTS the first sentence's claim. "Indeed" is used to give emphasis by adding specific evidence.

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "Indeed" — illustration/emphasis. Correct.
- **B)** "However" — contrast. Wrong.
- **C)** "Conversely" — contrast. Wrong.
- **D)** "Meanwhile" — time. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

### Section B.2: Add/Delete Questions

---

#### PROBLEM SET 12: ADD/DELETE (6 Problems)

---

**Problem 83: Relevance**

> **[1]** The Great Wall of China is one of the most ambitious construction projects in human history. **[2]** Built over several centuries, it stretches more than 13,000 miles. **[3]** The wall was originally constructed to protect against invasions from the north. **[4]** Today, it is one of the most popular tourist destinations in the world. **[5]** The Chinese government has invested heavily in its preservation.
>
> The writer would like to add the following sentence: "The construction of the wall required millions of workers and resulted in significant loss of life."

At which point should this sentence be added?

A) After sentence 1
B) After sentence 2
C) After sentence 3
D) After sentence 4

**Strategic Analysis:**

The proposed sentence discusses the human cost of construction (workers, loss of life). This is most relevant after sentence 2, which discusses the scale of the construction ("Built over several centuries, it stretches more than 13,000 miles"). The proposed sentence elaborates on the construction process.

- **A)** After sentence 1 — too early; the construction hasn't been discussed yet.
- **B)** After sentence 2 — follows naturally from the discussion of the wall's scale and construction.
- **C)** After sentence 3 — interrupts the flow from construction to purpose.
- **D)** After sentence 4 — too late; the topic has shifted to tourism.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 84: Deleting a Redundant Sentence**

> **[1]** The invention of the printing press revolutionized the spread of information. **[2]** Before the printing press, books were copied by hand, a laborious and time-consuming process. **[3]** Johannes Gutenberg invented the printing press around 1440. **[4]** The printing press was invented by Johannes Gutenberg in the mid-fifteenth century. **[5]** This innovation made books affordable and accessible to a wider audience.

The writer would like to delete sentence 4. Should the writer make this deletion?

A) Yes, because sentence 4 is grammatically incorrect.
B) Yes, because sentence 4 repeats information already stated in sentence 3.
C) No, because sentence 4 provides essential context about the printing press.
D) No, because sentence 4 introduces a new idea about the printing press.

**Strategic Analysis:**

Sentence 3: "Johannes Gutenberg invented the printing press around 1440."
Sentence 4: "The printing press was invented by Johannes Gutenberg in the mid-fifteenth century."

These two sentences convey the SAME information (Gutenberg invented the printing press, ~1440/mid-fifteenth century). Sentence 4 is redundant.

- **A)** Sentence 4 is grammatically correct. Wrong.
- **B)** Correct — sentence 4 repeats sentence 3.
- **C)** Sentence 4 does not provide essential context; it's redundant. Wrong.
- **D)** Sentence 4 does not introduce a new idea. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 85: Adding Supporting Detail**

> **[1]** Coral reefs are among the most biodiverse ecosystems on Earth. **[2]** They support thousands of marine species. **[3]** Unfortunately, coral reefs are under threat from climate change and ocean acidification.

The writer would like to add a sentence that provides a specific example of the threat mentioned in sentence 3. Which of the following would be most effective?

A) Coral reefs are found in tropical and subtropical waters around the world.
B) Rising ocean temperatures have caused widespread coral bleaching events in recent decades.
C) Many people enjoy snorkeling and diving near coral reefs.
D) Coral reefs are sometimes called the "rainforests of the sea."

**Strategic Analysis:**

The question asks for a sentence that provides a **specific example** of the threat mentioned in sentence 3 (climate change and ocean acidification).

- **A)** This sentence describes where coral reefs are found. It does not address the threat. Wrong.
- **B)** This sentence provides a specific example of a threat (rising ocean temperatures causing coral bleaching) that directly relates to climate change. Correct.
- **C)** This sentence describes human enjoyment of coral reefs. It does not address the threat. Wrong.
- **D)** This sentence provides a nickname for coral reefs. It does not address the threat. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 86: Deleting an Off-Topic Sentence**

> **[1]** The Industrial Revolution brought dramatic changes to European society. **[2]** Factories replaced cottage industries, drawing workers from rural areas into crowded cities. **[3]** These demographic shifts created new social classes and new forms of urban poverty. **[4]** The Renaissance, which preceded the Industrial Revolution by several centuries, was characterized by a flourishing of art and humanistic learning. **[5]** The working conditions in early factories were often dangerous and unsanitary.

The writer would like to delete sentence 4. Should the writer make this deletion?

A) Yes, because sentence 4 is grammatically incorrect.
B) Yes, because sentence 4 introduces information that is off-topic for a passage about the Industrial Revolution.
C) No, because sentence 4 provides essential historical context for understanding the Industrial Revolution.
D) No, because sentence 4 introduces a new idea that is developed in the following sentences.

**Strategic Analysis:**

The passage is about the **Industrial Revolution** — its social and economic impacts. Sentence 4 discusses the **Renaissance**, which is a different historical period. While the Renaissance preceded the Industrial Revolution, it is not directly relevant to the passage's focus on industrialization, urbanization, and working conditions.

- **A)** Sentence 4 is grammatically correct. Wrong.
- **B)** Correct — sentence 4 introduces information about the Renaissance, which is off-topic for a passage focused on the Industrial Revolution.
- **C)** The Renaissance is not essential context for understanding the Industrial Revolution's social impacts. Wrong.
- **D)** Sentence 5 returns to the Industrial Revolution topic, not the Renaissance. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 87: Adding a Transition Sentence**

> **[1]** The company's profits declined sharply in the third quarter. **[2]** Several factors contributed to this downturn. **[3]** Consumer spending decreased due to rising inflation. **[4]** Supply chain disruptions increased production costs. **[5]** The company's main competitor launched a successful new product line.

The writer would like to add a sentence between sentences 4 and 5 that transitions from internal factors to external factors. Which of the following would be most effective?

A) These internal challenges were compounded by external pressures.
B) The company's CEO announced her retirement in September.
C) Consumer confidence remained low throughout the quarter.
D) The company had faced similar challenges in previous years.

**Strategic Analysis:**

Sentences 3 and 4 discuss **internal factors** (consumer spending, supply chain disruptions). Sentence 5 discusses an **external factor** (competitor's new product). The writer wants a transition sentence that signals this shift.

- **A)** "These internal challenges were compounded by external pressures." — This explicitly signals the transition from internal to external factors. Correct.
- **B)** The CEO's retirement is neither clearly internal nor external, and it doesn't transition to the competitor point. Wrong.
- **C)** Consumer confidence is related to internal factors (consumer spending), not a transition to external factors. Wrong.
- **D)** Previous challenges don't transition to the competitor point. Wrong.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 88: Evaluating Whether to Add a Sentence**

> **[1]** The ancient city of Petra, located in modern-day Jordan, was once a thriving center of trade. **[2]** Carved directly into rose-colored sandstone cliffs, the city's architecture is remarkable. **[3]** The Nabataeans, who built Petra, were skilled engineers and traders. **[4]** Today, Petra is a UNESCO World Heritage Site and a popular tourist destination.

The writer is considering adding the following sentence after sentence 2: "The city was eventually abandoned and remained hidden from the Western world for centuries."

Should the writer add this sentence?

A) Yes, because it provides important historical context about Petra's decline.
B) Yes, because it explains why Petra is a UNESCO World Heritage Site.
C) No, because it disrupts the passage's focus on Petra's architectural significance.
D) No, because it introduces information that is not developed in the surrounding sentences.

**Strategic Analysis:**

The passage describes Petra's history (trade center), its architecture, its builders (Nabataeans), and its current status (UNESCO site, tourist destination). The proposed sentence discusses Petra's abandonment and hidden history.

While this information is interesting, the passage does not develop this idea further. Sentence 3 returns to the Nabataeans, and sentence 4 discusses Petra's current status. The proposed sentence would introduce an undeveloped tangent.

- **A)** While the information is historically interesting, it's not developed in the passage. This is not a strong enough reason to add it.
- **B)** The proposed sentence does not explain why Petra is a UNESCO site. Wrong.
- **C)** The passage covers more than just architecture (trade, Nabataeans, tourism), so this is not the best reason.
- **D)** Correct — the proposed sentence introduces information (abandonment, hidden history) that is not developed in the surrounding sentences. The passage moves from architecture to Nabataeans to current status without addressing the abandonment.

**Answer: D**

---

### Section B.3: Author Intent and Writer's Goal

---

#### PROBLEM SET 13: AUTHOR INTENT (6 Problems)

---

**Problem 89: Identifying the Purpose of a Sentence**

> **[1]** The discovery of penicillin by Alexander Fleming in 1928 revolutionized modern medicine. **[2]** Before penicillin, even minor infections could be fatal. **[3]** Fleming noticed that a mold called *Penicillium notatum* had killed bacteria in a petri dish. **[4]** This accidental observation led to the development of the first antibiotic. **[5]** By World War II, penicillin was being mass-produced to treat wounded soldiers.

The author includes sentence 3 ("Fleming noticed that a mold...") in order to:

A) explain the scientific mechanism by which penicillin kills bacteria.
B) describe the accidental nature of Fleming's discovery.
C) argue that scientific breakthroughs are always the result of luck.
D) compare Fleming's methods to those of other scientists.

**Strategic Analysis:**

Sentence 3 describes what Fleming observed — a mold killed bacteria. This observation was accidental (as stated in sentence 4: "This accidental observation..."). The purpose of sentence 3 is to describe the specific observation that led to the discovery.

- **A)** Sentence 3 does not explain the scientific mechanism — it only describes what Fleming noticed. Wrong.
- **B)** Correct — sentence 3 describes the accidental observation that led to the discovery, supporting the idea that the discovery was unplanned.
- **C)** The passage does not make a general argument about all scientific breakthroughs. Wrong.
- **D)** The passage does not compare Fleming to other scientists. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 90: Identifying the Purpose of a Paragraph**

> **[1]** The Great Barrier Reef is the world's largest coral reef system, stretching over 2,300 kilometers along the coast of Australia. **[2]** It is home to an extraordinary diversity of marine life, including over 1,500 species of fish and 400 types of coral. **[3]** The reef also supports dugongs, sea turtles, and numerous species of sharks and rays. **[4]** This biodiversity makes the reef not only ecologically significant but also economically valuable, as it supports tourism and fishing industries.

The author's primary purpose in this paragraph is to:

A) argue for the protection of the Great Barrier Reef.
B) describe the ecological and economic importance of the Great Barrier Reef.
C) explain the formation of coral reef ecosystems.
D) compare the Great Barrier Reef to other reef systems.

**Strategic Analysis:**

The paragraph describes the Great Barrier Reef's size, its biodiversity (fish, coral, dugongs, etc.), and concludes by stating that this biodiversity makes it ecologically significant and economically valuable.

- **A)** The paragraph does not make an argument for protection. Wrong.
- **B)** Correct — the paragraph describes the reef's biodiversity (ecological importance) and mentions its economic value.
- **C)** The paragraph does not explain how coral reefs form. Wrong.
- **D)** The paragraph does not compare the Great Barrier Reef to other reefs. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 91: Selecting the Best Sentence to Achieve a Goal**

> The writer wants to add a sentence to the passage that emphasizes the urgency of addressing climate change. Which of the following sentences would best achieve this goal?

A) Climate change is a complex phenomenon that scientists have been studying for decades.
B) The effects of climate change are already being felt around the world, and without immediate action, these effects will become irreversible.
C) Some scientists disagree about the primary causes of climate change.
D) Climate change was first identified as a potential problem in the late twentieth century.

**Strategic Analysis:**

The goal is to **emphasize the urgency** of addressing climate change.

- **A)** This sentence describes the complexity of climate change but does not emphasize urgency. Wrong.
- **B)** This sentence states that effects are already occurring and that immediate action is needed to prevent irreversible consequences. This emphasizes urgency. Correct.
- **C)** This sentence mentions scientific disagreement, which does not emphasize urgency. Wrong.
- **D)** This sentence provides historical context but does not emphasize urgency. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 92: Identifying the Author's Tone**

> **[1]** The proposal to replace the historic library with a modern office building has sparked considerable controversy. **[2]** Proponents argue that the new building would bring economic development to the area. **[3]** Opponents counter that the library is an irreplaceable cultural landmark. **[4]** The city council will vote on the proposal next month.

The tone of this passage can best be described as:

A) passionate and indignant.
B) objective and informative.
C) nostalgic and reflective.
D) skeptical and critical.

**Strategic Analysis:**

The passage presents both sides of a controversy (proponents and opponents) without taking a side. It concludes by stating a factual next step (the city council will vote). The tone is balanced and factual.

- **A)** The passage does not express passion or indignation. Wrong.
- **B)** Correct — the passage presents information objectively without taking a side.
- **C)** The passage does not express nostalgia or reflection. Wrong.
- **D)** The passage does not express skepticism or criticism toward either side. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 93: Selecting the Best Concluding Sentence**

> **[1]** The invention of the telephone by Alexander Graham Bell in 1876 transformed communication. **[2]** Before the telephone, long-distance communication was limited to written letters and telegraph messages. **[3]** The telephone allowed people to speak directly with each other across great distances. **[4]** Over time, telephone technology evolved from rotary dials to touch-tones to mobile phones.

Which of the following sentences would best conclude the passage by summarizing the main idea?

A) Alexander Graham Bell was a prolific inventor who held numerous patents.
B) The telephone's development illustrates how technological innovations can fundamentally reshape human interaction.
C) Many people today rely on smartphones for both communication and entertainment.
D) The telegraph, which preceded the telephone, was invented by Samuel Morse.

**Strategic Analysis:**

The passage traces the telephone's invention and evolution, emphasizing its transformative impact on communication. The best concluding sentence should summarize this main idea.

- **A)** This sentence provides additional information about Bell but does not summarize the passage's main idea about the telephone's impact. Wrong.
- **B)** Correct — this sentence summarizes the passage's main idea about how the telephone reshaped human interaction.
- **C)** This sentence introduces a new point (smartphones today) rather than summarizing the passage. Wrong.
- **D)** This sentence provides historical context about the telegraph but does not summarize the passage. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 94: Identifying the Purpose of a Specific Detail**

> **[1]** The monarch butterfly's annual migration is one of the most spectacular natural phenomena in North America. **[2]** Each fall, millions of monarchs travel up to 3,000 miles from Canada and the United States to central Mexico. **[3]** The butterflies cluster together on oyamel fir trees, creating a breathtaking display of orange and black. **[4]** This migration is essential to the monarchs' survival, as the mild Mexican climate allows them to survive the winter.

The author includes the detail about the oyamel fir trees in sentence 3 in order to:

A) explain why monarchs migrate to Mexico.
B) describe the visual spectacle of the monarchs' clustering behavior.
C) argue for the conservation of the oyamel fir forest.
D) compare the monarch migration to other animal migrations.

**Strategic Analysis:**

Sentence 3 describes the butterflies clustering on oyamel fir trees and calls it "a breathtaking display of orange and black." The detail about the trees is part of the description of the visual spectacle.

- **A)** The reason monarchs migrate to Mexico is explained in sentence 4 (mild climate), not sentence 3. Wrong.
- **B)** Correct — the detail about the oyamel fir trees is part of the description of the visual spectacle of the monarchs' clustering.
- **C)** The passage does not make an argument for conservation. Wrong.
- **D)** The passage does not compare the monarch migration to other migrations. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

### Section B.4: Sentence Placement and Organization

---

#### PROBLEM SET 14: SENTENCE PLACEMENT (6 Problems)

---

**Problem 95: Placing a Sentence in a Paragraph**

> **[1]** The process of photosynthesis is essential to life on Earth. **[2]** Plants use sunlight, carbon dioxide, and water to produce glucose and oxygen. **[3]** This glucose serves as the primary energy source for the plant. **[4]** The oxygen produced is released into the atmosphere, where it is used by other organisms for respiration.
>
> The writer would like to add the following sentence: "Without photosynthesis, most life forms on Earth would not survive."

At which point should this sentence be placed?

A) After sentence 1
B) After sentence 2
C) After sentence 3
D) After sentence 4

**Strategic Analysis:**

The proposed sentence states the importance of photosynthesis to life on Earth. This is a general statement that would logically follow sentence 1, which introduces photosynthesis as essential to life. The proposed sentence reinforces this point before the passage explains how photosynthesis works.

- **A)** After sentence 1 — this placement reinforces the importance of photosynthesis before the detailed explanation. Correct.
- **B)** After sentence 2 — this would interrupt the explanation of how photosynthesis works.
- **C)** After sentence 3 — this would interrupt the explanation of glucose and oxygen.
- **D)** After sentence 4 — this would be an odd placement after the explanation is complete.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 96: Identifying the Best Order for Sentences**

> The writer wants to rearrange the sentences in the following paragraph to improve its logical flow. Which of the following represents the most logical order?
>
> **Sentence A:** The city's population doubled in just twenty years.
> **Sentence B:** The discovery of gold in 1848 triggered a massive influx of settlers to California.
> **Sentence C:** This rapid growth strained the city's infrastructure and led to housing shortages.
> **Sentence D:** San Francisco, once a small town, was transformed almost overnight.

A) B, A, D, C
B) B, D, A, C
C) D, B, A, C
D) A, B, C, D

**Strategic Analysis:**

The logical flow should be:
1. **B** — The discovery of gold triggered an influx of settlers (the cause).
2. **D** — San Francisco was transformed (the general effect).
3. **A** — The population doubled (a specific effect of the transformation).
4. **C** — This growth strained infrastructure (a consequence of the population doubling).

- **A)** B, A, D, C — This order places the population doubling before the general transformation, which is less logical.
- **B)** B, D, A, C — Correct. The cause (gold discovery) leads to the general effect (transformation), then the specific effect (population doubling), then the consequence (infrastructure strain).
- **C)** D, B, A, C — This order starts with the transformation before explaining the cause, which is less logical.
- **D)** A, B, C, D — This order starts with the population doubling before explaining the cause, which is illogical.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 97: Placing a Sentence with a Pronoun Reference**

> **[1]** The ancient library of Alexandria was one of the greatest repositories of knowledge in the ancient world. **[2]** It housed hundreds of thousands of scrolls covering subjects from philosophy to mathematics. **[3]** Scholars from across the Mediterranean traveled to study there. **[4]** Its destruction resulted in the loss of countless irreplaceable texts.
>
> The writer would like to add the following sentence: "The library was founded in the third century BCE by Ptolemy I."

At which point should this sentence be placed?

A) After sentence 1
B) After sentence 2
C) After sentence 3
D) After sentence 4

**Strategic Analysis:**

The proposed sentence provides historical information about the library's founding. This is background information that should come after the introduction of the library (sentence 1) but before the details about its contents and significance.

- **A)** After sentence 1 — this placement provides historical context after the library is introduced. Correct.
- **B)** After sentence 2 — this would interrupt the description of the library's contents.
- **C)** After sentence 3 — this would interrupt the discussion of scholars and destruction.
- **D)** After sentence 4 — this would be too late; the passage has already discussed the library's destruction.

**Answer: A**

---

**Problem 98: Identifying a Misplaced Sentence**

> **[1]** The Industrial Revolution brought sweeping changes to European society. **[2]** Factories replaced cottage industries, drawing workers from rural areas into crowded cities. **[3]** The term "revolution" implies rapid, dramatic transformation. **[4]** These demographic shifts created new social classes and new forms of urban poverty.

Which sentence is misplaced in this paragraph?

A) Sentence 1
B) Sentence 2
C) Sentence 3
D) Sentence 4

**Strategic Analysis:**

The paragraph's main topic is the social changes brought by the Industrial Revolution. Sentences 1, 2, and 4 all discuss these changes. Sentence 3, however, defines the term "revolution" — this is a tangential point that disrupts the flow of the paragraph.

- **A)** Sentence 1 introduces the topic. It is not misplaced.
- **B)** Sentence 2 describes a specific change. It is not misplaced.
- **C)** Sentence 3 defines "revolution" — this is off-topic and disrupts the flow. Misplaced.
- **D)** Sentence 4 describes the consequences of the demographic shifts. It is not misplaced.

**Answer: C**

---

**Problem 99: Placing a Transition Sentence**

> **[1]** The company's revenue increased by 15% in the first quarter. **[2]** This growth was driven by strong demand for the company's flagship product. **[3]** The company's expenses also rose significantly during the same period. **[4]** Higher raw material costs and increased marketing spending contributed to this rise. **[5]** Despite the increased expenses, the company's profit margin improved.

The writer would like to add a sentence between sentences 2 and 3 that signals a shift from revenue to expenses. Which of the following would be most effective?

A) The company's flagship product has been on the market for five years.
B) However, the company's financial success was not without its challenges.
C) The company plans to launch a new product line next quarter.
D) Revenue growth is the most important indicator of a company's health.

**Strategic Analysis:**

Sentences 1 and 2 discuss **revenue growth**. Sentences 3 and 4 discuss **rising expenses**. The writer wants a sentence that signals this shift.

- **A)** This sentence provides additional information about the flagship product but does not signal a shift to expenses. Wrong.
- **B)** "However, the company's financial success was not without its challenges." — This signals a shift from positive news (revenue growth) to challenges (rising expenses). Correct.
- **C)** This sentence introduces a new topic (new product line) rather than transitioning to expenses. Wrong.
- **D)** This sentence makes a general statement about revenue but does not transition to expenses. Wrong.

**Answer: B**

---

**Problem 100: Evaluating Paragraph Organization**

> **[1]** The migration of monarch butterflies is one of nature's most remarkable phenomena. **[2]** Each fall, millions of monarchs travel up to 3,000 miles from Canada and the United States to central Mexico. **[3]** The butterflies cluster together on oyamel fir trees, creating a breathtaking display. **[4]** Scientists have studied this migration for decades, but many questions remain unanswered. **[5]** One mystery is how the butterflies navigate such vast distances with precision.

The writer is considering moving sentence 5 to the beginning of the paragraph. Would this improve the paragraph's organization?

A) Yes, because it introduces the main idea of the paragraph.
B) Yes, because it creates a more engaging opening for the paragraph.
C) No, because the paragraph already has a clear topic sentence.
D) No, because sentence 5 refers to "one mystery" that has not yet been introduced.

**Strategic Analysis:**

Sentence 1 is a clear topic sentence that introduces the monarch butterfly migration. Sentence 5 refers to "one mystery" — this phrase requires context that the migration has been studied but questions remain (sentence 4). Moving sentence 5 to the beginning would leave "one mystery" without a clear referent.

- **A)** Sentence 5 does not introduce the main idea; sentence 1 does. Wrong.
- **B)** While sentence 5 might be engaging, moving it would disrupt the logical flow. Wrong.
- **C)** The paragraph does have a clear topic sentence, but this is not the primary reason not to move sentence 5.
- **D)** Correct — sentence 5 refers to "one mystery" that has not yet been introduced if moved to the beginning. The phrase "one mystery" requires the context provided by sentence 4.

**Answer: D**

## PART C: KNOWLEDGE OF LANGUAGE — STYLE AND DICTION

### Section C.1: Word Choice and Precision

---

#### PROBLEM SET 15: WORD CHOICE (8 Problems)

---

**Problem 101: "Affect" vs. "Effect"**

> The new policy had a significant **affect** on employee morale.

A) NO CHANGE
B) effect
C) affected
D) effected

**Strategic Analysis:**

- "Affect" (verb) = to influence
- "Effect" (noun) = a result

In this sentence, we need a noun (following "a significant"): "a significant effect on employee morale."

- **A) NO CHANGE:** "affect" is a verb, but we
